# Excalidraw Data
## Text Elements
Trees ^j6amnZDW

- Tree data structure is a hierarchical structure that is used to represent 
  and organize data in a way that is easy to navigate and search. It is a 
  collection of nodes that are connected by edges and has a hierarchical 
  relationship between the nodes.  ^EfVsEye3

Why?
-> Add, remove & find in O(log(n)) time.
-> Ordered storage (insertion and deletion).
-> Cost effective (dynamic in nature). ^l80p6673

Binary tree : 
-> Hierarchical data structure.
-> Parent node has 2 child nodes.
-> Should be balanced to give log(n)
    operational time complexity, else 
    in case of unbalanced binary search 
    tree gives O(n) time complexity.  ^rsMPmpin

- With self-balancing binary tress we can solve the problem of binary tree.
    but binary tree is also inefficient for sorted data. ^P8MNVZ8J

unbalanced 
binary tree ^XAF1FbCS

Where are binary tree's used ?
-> File systems.
-> Data Bases 
-> Algorithms/Networking
-> Math
-> Decision trees 
-> Compression of files - Huffman Coding
-> Heaps, Graphs, etc... ^eardhTXG

Structure :  ^k1cZ3uSr

5 ^BwPa9Yn0

6 ^zju5yvuX

8 ^lIhpp8Z4

14 ^0aTdDIzA

3 ^0lfjeLuP

9 ^WFSgz1Wr

11 ^ZtVfXY3X

15 ^1CwSyd0W

4 ^JD1Og1UL

siblings ^fTrvrI02

leaf ^ffzFsQAo

Binary tree :
    int value
    Node left
    Node right ^cnkOFFSu

Properties :
- Size : number of nodes 
- Child & parent
- Siblings
- Degree : num of edges/children
- Edge
- Height : max number of edges b/w 2 nodes
- Leaf node : lowest node
- Level node :  subtract height of root to 
    height of node => root height - node height
    (height root = 0).
- Ancestor and descendent ^xU6pevDw

leaf ^ebuKNHLg

leaf ^g9K1sWBJ

leaf ^2QeY0Ea4

every node has 1 child only ^LQPqWcKW

Properties that will help in some questions : ^cfMMRTgt

- Perfect Binary tree : height = h,
    Total Nodes = 2^(n+1) -1 

- Total number of Leaf nodes in perfect 
    binary tree :  2^n
    total nodes = 2^h -1 

- N = number of leaves, then 
    log (n+1) levels at least    
  N = number of nodes, then 
    log(n+1) minimum nodes

- Strict binary tree, n = leaf nodes
    n-1 => internal nodes 
number of leaf nodes = number of internal nodes + 1

- Number of leaf nodes = 1 + number of internal nodes 
    with 2 children  ^p6lNsy9L

Trees can be implemented in 2 ways:
- Linked representation (majority of cases)
- Array representation (heap, segment trees, etc) ^CB3B8cgP

Implementation of Trees ^3KGsBuex

This can be achieved with following data structures :
- Linked representation  
- Sequential representation (using arrays) ^R72VEG3j

5 ^JSfthJsV

6 ^Im7qynFT

8 ^84HDXkE6

9 ^YRTtW4Hg

11 ^cBOtdQkw

null ^fHj0sh0Z

Sequential :- 

[5, 6, 8, 9, null, null, 11] ^bpiDcDfa

Linked :- ^zQuOTdgY

Height :- 
- n = 2^h 
- log n = h.log(2)
- h = log[base 2] * (n) ^mzpiKmyu

AVL Trees ^6RkizZxB

- Adelson-Velsky and Landis tree, is a self balancing binary tree that eliminates 
  the problem of chaining in binary tree. Due to chaining the operations which
  were gonna take log(n) time for operations now take n. AVL trees says for 
  every single node the height of left and right tree should not be more than 1. ^YFbq8ATF

- For every node :
height(left) - height(right), can only be -1, +1 or 0 ^B7xWqwbf
